## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: classical mechanics — nonlinear oscillations / dynamical systems
**Analysis**: The target dv_dt is acceleration of an oscillator with state variables x (position) and v (velocity) evolving in time t, which is the standard phase-space formulation of nonlinear second-order ODEs (e.g., Duffing, pendulum, Van der Pol) possibly with damping and external/parametric forcing.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear (undriven) harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x (conservative linear restoring force)
- Linear damping oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v (viscous damping proportional to velocity)
- Driven damped oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v + c2 * cos(c3 * t) (external periodic forcing)
- Duffing (cubic stiffness) oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 (hardening/softening spring nonlinearity)
- Duffing with damping and drive: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (canonical forced nonlinear oscillator)
- Nonlinear drag (quadratic): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v * Abs(v) (aerodynamic-like dissipation)
- Nonlinear drag (cubic): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v**3 (odd-power dissipative nonlinearity)
- Simple pendulum (geometric nonlinearity): dv_dt = -c0 * sin(c1 * x) - c2 * v (restoring torque ~ sin(angle))
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * (1 - c1 * x**2) * v - c2 * x (state-dependent damping leading to limit cycles)
- Rayleigh oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * (1 - c1 * v**2) * v - c2 * x (velocity-dependent damping leading to self-oscillation)
- Parametric stiffness modulation: dv_dt = -(c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x - c3 * v (Mathieu-type parametric excitation)
- Nonlinear saturating restoring force: dv_dt = -c0 * x / (1 + c1 * x**2) - c2 * v (effective stiffness decreases/increases with amplitude)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Conservative oscillator signature: dv_dt depends primarily on x (not explicitly on t), and the restoring term is typically an odd function of x (e.g., -x, -x - x**3, -sin(x)).
- Viscous damping signature: a term proportional to -v; energy decreases monotonically in the absence of forcing.
- Nonlinear dissipation signature: odd powers of v (v**3) or v*Abs(v) indicating amplitude-dependent damping (stronger losses at large speeds).
- Hardening vs softening stiffness: inclusion of -x**3 with sign determining whether oscillation frequency increases or decreases with amplitude.
- Geometric nonlinearity / bounded restoring: sin(c*x) suggests a pendulum-like restoring force and predicts period increase with amplitude.
- Self-excited oscillation (limit cycle) signature: state-dependent damping such as (1 - c*x**2)*v or (1 - c*v**2)*v producing negative damping at small amplitude and positive damping at large amplitude.
- External periodic forcing signature: additive terms like cos(c*t) or sin(c*t), often producing resonance/beat phenomena.
- Parametric excitation signature: multiplicative time dependence on x (e.g., x*cos(c*t)), associated with parametric resonance regions rather than direct forcing.

GT: F0*sin(t) - alpha*v**c0 - omega0**c1*(gamma*Abs(v)**c2 + c3)*x - omega0**c4*x
Candidate formulas: 50

GT (fixed) is:
\[
-0.0230405406738805\,v^3\;-\;1.1056075693807\,x\,(0.0552411020531317\,|v|^{1/3}+1)\;-\;1.1056075693807\,x\;+\;0.350781823399691\sin(t).
\]
Key structural requirements:
- Has a **\(\sin(t)\)** term with **constant amplitude** (not divided by \(c+t\)).
- Has a **\(v^3\)** term with constant coefficient.
- Has an **\(x|v|^{1/3}\)** term (because \(x(0.05524|v|^{1/3}+1)\) expands to \(0.06108\,x|v|^{1/3}+1.1056\,x\)).
- No rational-in-\(t\) prefactors like \(1/(c+t)\) anywhere.
- Uses **Abs(v)** in a non-integer power; this cannot be replaced by \(v^{1/3}\) globally because \(v\) can be negative.

Now check candidates.

### Candidates 1–3
All are sums of: terms like \( \frac{\text{(stuff)}}{c1+t}\), plus \(x^3\), plus \(v^3\), plus cosines (also divided by \(c1+t\)), plus possibly \(c9 x\).
- They **cannot produce** an \(x|v|^{1/3}\) term at all (no Abs, no fractional power of \(v\), no \(x\cdot f(v)\) except via \(t x/(c+t)\)).
- They also only have trig as **cos(...) /(c+t)**, not a plain \(\sin(t)\) term. You cannot choose constants to remove the denominator for all \(t\).
⇒ Not match.

### Candidates 4, 6
Form: \(c0 x + \frac{(\text{constants + cos})}{c2+t} + c4 x^3 + c5 v^3 + \frac{c9 x}{c2+t}\) (and candidate 6 also has \(c4 t/(c2+t)\)).
- Again **no \(x|v|^{1/3}\)** term.
- Trig appears only divided by \(c2+t\), so cannot equal \(0.35078\sin t\) globally.
⇒ Not match.

### Candidates 5, 8
Similar to 1 but with an added constant \(c3\) (or \(c3\) not divided).
- Still **no \(x|v|^{1/3}\)**.
- Trig only as cos/(c+t).
⇒ Not match.

### Candidates 7
Has \(c2\) constant and \(c9 x\) (no denominator on \(x\)), but still:
- **no \(x|v|^{1/3}\)**.
- trig only cos/(c+t).
⇒ Not match.

### Candidates 9–10
Have \(c0 x + c1 + c2 x^3 + \frac{c3 t}{c4+t} + c5 v^3 + \frac{\cos}{c4+t} + \frac{c9 x}{c4+t}\) (10 has \(t v^3/(c4+t)\)).
- **no \(x|v|^{1/3}\)**.
- trig only divided by \(c4+t\).
- extra rational-in-\(t\) terms cannot be removed except by setting their coefficients to 0, but even then you still lack the \(x|v|^{1/3}\) and \(\sin t\).
⇒ Not match.

### Candidates 11–17
Include variants with \(t v^3/(c+t)\) and constants/(c+t).
- Any \(t v^3/(c+t)\) cannot equal a pure \(v^3\) term for all \(t\) unless coefficient is 0; then you still only have \(v^3\) possibly (some candidates do have plain \(v^3\), others only \(t v^3/(c+t)\)).
- None contain **Abs(v)** or \(v^{1/3}\), so **cannot make \(x|v|^{1/3}\)**.
- Trig still appears as cos/(c+t), not plain sin.
⇒ Not match.

### Candidates 18–21
Introduce \(t x^3/(c+t)\) etc.
- Still **no \(x|v|^{1/3}\)**.
- Still no plain \(\sin(t)\).
⇒ Not match.

### Candidates 22, 33, 44
Have \(c3*x**c4\) (a power of \(x\)), plus trig/(c+t), plus \(t v^3/(c+t)\) (22,33) or plain \(v^3\) (44).
- Even with free exponent \(c4\), this only creates \(x^{c4}\), not \(x|v|^{1/3}\).
- No Abs(v) anywhere.
- Trig still divided by \(c+t\).
⇒ Not match.

### Candidates 23–31, 35, 39–43
These are mixtures of \(x^3\) terms (some divided by \(c+t\)), \(t x^3/(c+t)\), \(v^3\) or \(t v^3/(c+t)\), and cos/(c+t), plus possibly \(c9 x\) or \(c9 x/(c+t)\).
- None can generate the essential coupling term \(x|v|^{1/3}\).
- None have an undivided \(\sin(t)\); all trig is cos/(c+t).
- Any attempt to “fake” \(\sin(t)\) via phase shift from cosine fails because of the unavoidable \(1/(c+t)\) factor.
⇒ Not match.

### Candidates 32, 41, 47
These have a similar “everything over (c+t)” structure plus some linear \(x\) term.
- Still **no Abs(v)** and no fractional power of \(v\).
- Trig divided by \(c+t\).
⇒ Not match.

### Candidates 34, 36–37, 45–46, 49
These are the “\(c0 x + \frac{...}{c2+t}\)” family, with \(x^3\) or \(x^{c4}\), and \(v^3\) or \(t v^3/(c2+t)\), and cos/(c2+t).
- Still **no \(x|v|^{1/3}\)**.
- Still no plain \(\sin(t)\).
⇒ Not match.

### Candidates 48, 50
More variants with \(t x/(c+t)\), \(x^3\), \(t v^3/(c+t)\), cos/(c+t), etc.
- Still **no \(x|v|^{1/3}\)**.
- Still no plain \(\sin(t)\).
⇒ Not match.

### Overall decisive obstruction (applies to all 50)
1) **Missing \(x|v|^{1/3}\) term**: GT contains \(x\cdot |v|^{1/3}\). None of the candidates include Abs(v) or any fractional power of \(v\), nor any multiplicative coupling \(x f(v)\) that could be tuned into \(x|v|^{1/3}\). This alone prevents equivalence on a domain where \(v\) can be negative.

2) **Trig structure mismatch**: GT has an undivided \(0.35078\sin(t)\). All candidates only have cosine terms divided by \((c+t)\) or \((c2+t)\). No constant choice makes \(\cos(\cdot)/(c+t)\) equal to \(\sin(t)\) for all \(t\).

Therefore no candidate can be made mathematically equivalent to the GT by parameter choice.

GT Equivalence Verification (PO4)
============================================================
GT: F0*sin(t) - alpha*v**c0 - omega0**c1*(gamma*Abs(v)**c2 + c3)*x - omega0**c4*x
Candidates evaluated: 50
Matched candidate IDs: []
Matched candidates: []

I need to analyze whether each candidate can be made equivalent to the Ground Truth (GT):

**GT:** `-0.0230405406738805*v**3 - 1.1056075693807*x*(0.0552411020531317*Abs(v)**0.333333333333333 + 1) - 1.1056075693807*x + 0.350781823399691*sin(t)`

Expanding: `-0.0230405*v³ - 0.06107*|v|^(1/3)*x - 1.10561*x - 1.10561*x + 0.35078*sin(t)`
= `-0.0230405*v³ - 0.06107*|v|^(1/3)*x - 2.21121*x + 0.35078*sin(t)`

The GT has these basis functions:
1. `v³` 
2. `|v|^(1/3) * x` (product of |v|^(1/3) and x)
3. `x` (linear)
4. `sin(t)`

Key observations:
- The GT contains `|v|^(1/3) * x`, which is a very specific nonlinear term
- The GT contains `sin(t)`, not `cos(t)` (though `cos(t + c) = sin(t)` with appropriate phase shift)
- No `x³` term in GT (coefficient is 0 would need to be possible)
- No `1/(c+t)` dependence in GT

Now let me analyze the candidates. All candidates contain terms like `1/(c1+t)`, `t/(c1+t)`, `cos(t)/(c1+t)`, `cos(c7*t)/(c1+t)`, etc. The critical question is: can these be made to produce `sin(t)` and eliminate the `1/(c+t)` dependence?

**Critical issue:** The GT has `sin(t)` as a standalone term, not divided by anything. The candidates have `cos(t)/(c1+t)` and `cos(c7*t)/(c1+t)`. These cannot produce a standalone `sin(t)` — they always have the `1/(c1+t)` factor. Setting `c1 = 0` would give `cos(t)/t`, which is NOT `sin(t)`.

**Second critical issue:** The GT has `|v|^(1/3) * x`. None of the candidates contain `|v|^(1/3)` or any fractional power of `v` multiplied by `x`. The candidates have `v³`, `x³`, `x^c4`, but never `|v|^(1/3)*x`.

**Can we set `c1 → ∞`?** No — that would zero out all the `/(c1+t)` terms, losing the trig terms entirely.

**Can any candidate produce `|v|^(1/3)*x`?** Looking through all candidates, none have a term like `|v|^c * x`. Some have `x^c4` (Candidates 22, 33, 44, 45, 46), but that's a power of x, not v.

Since the GT requires `|v|^(1/3)*x` and `sin(t)` as basis functions, and NO candidate contains either:
- A term proportional to `|v|^(fractional power) * x`
- A standalone `sin(t)` or `cos(t)` (all trig terms are divided by `(c+t)`)

No candidate can match the GT.

Let me verify: could we approximate by ignoring the `|v|^(1/3)*x` term? No — the rules explicitly forbid approximations. The coefficient `0.06107` is nonzero.

Candidate 1 verdict: [NO MATCH]
